# Surah 7 — Al-Araf

## 7:1-3 — verses 1-3 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Tafsir of Surat al-A'raf

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

The discussion concerning the disconnected letters, their elaboration, and the disagreement of people about them, has already preceded at the beginning of Surat al-Baqarah.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] from Ibn Abbas concerning {Alif Lam Mim Sad}: "I am Allah, I distinguish (afsilu)." Sa'id ibn Jubayr said likewise.

His saying, {A Book has been sent down to you}, means: this is a Book sent down to you, that is, from your Lord. {So let there be no constraint in your breast concerning it}. Mujahid, Ata, Qatadah, and al-Suddi said: meaning, no doubt concerning it.

It has also been said: do not feel constrained in conveying it and in warning by means of it, and be patient as the resolute ones among the messengers were patient. This is why He said, {that you may warn thereby}, meaning: it was sent down to you so that you may warn the disbelievers by it, {and as a reminder to the believers}.

Then the Exalted said, addressing all of creation: {Follow what has been sent down to you from your Lord}, meaning: follow the footsteps of the unlettered Prophet who brought you a Book sent down to you from the Lord and Sovereign of all things. {And do not follow, besides Him, any allies}, meaning: do not depart from what the Messenger brought you toward anything else, for then you would have turned away from the judgment of Allah toward the judgment of someone other than Him.

{Little do you take heed}, similar to His saying: {And most of the people, even if you desire it eagerly, are not believers} [Yusuf: 103], and His saying: {And if you obey most of those upon the earth, they will lead you astray from the path of Allah} [al-An'am: 116], and His saying: {And most of them do not believe in Allah except while they associate partners with Him} [Yusuf: 106].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

تَفْسِيرُ سُورَةِ الْأَعْرَافِ

بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ

* *

قَدْ تَقَدَّمَ الْكَلَامُ فِي أَوَّلِ "سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ" عَلَى مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْحُرُوفِ وَبَسْطُهُ، وَاخْتِلَافُ النَّاسِ فِيهِ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانُ بْنُ وَكِيع، حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، عَنْ شَرِيك، عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ السَّائِبِ، عَنْ أَبِي الضُّحَى، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿المص﴾ أَنَا اللَّهُ أَفْصِلُ وَكَذَا قَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَير.

[قَوْلُهُ] ﴿كِتَابٌ أُنزلَ إِلَيْكَ﴾ أَيْ: هَذَا كِتَابٌ أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ، أَيْ: مِنْ رَبِّكَ، ﴿فَلا يَكُنْ فِي صَدْرِكَ حَرَجٌ مِنْهُ﴾ قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، [وَعَطَاءٌ] وَقَتَادَةُ والسُّدِّي: شَكٌّ مِنْهُ.

وَقِيلَ: لَا تَتَحَرَّجْ بِهِ فِي إِبْلَاغِهِ وَالْإِنْذَارِ بِهِ [وَاصْبِرْ] كَمَا صَبَرَ أُولُو الْعَزْمِ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿لِتُنْذِرَ بِهِ﴾ أَيْ: أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ لِتُنْذِرَ بِهِ الْكَافِرِينَ، ﴿وَذِكْرَى لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ .

ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى مُخَاطِبًا لِلْعَالَمِ: ﴿اتَّبِعُوا مَا أُنزلَ إِلَيْكُمْ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ﴾ أَيِ: اقْتَفُوا آثَارَ النَّبِيِّ الْأُمِّيِّ الَّذِي جَاءَكُمْ بِكِتَابٍ أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكُمْ مِنْ رَبِّ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَمَلِيكِهِ، ﴿وَلا تَتَّبِعُوا مِنْ دُونِهِ أَوْلِيَاءَ﴾ أَيْ: لَا تَخْرُجُوا عَمَّا جَاءَكُمْ بِهِ الرَّسُولُ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، فَتَكُونُوا قَدْ عَدَلْتُمْ عَنْ حُكْمِ اللَّهِ إِلَى حُكْمِ غَيْرِهِ.

﴿قَلِيلا مَا تَذَكَّرُونَ﴾ كَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَمَا أَكْثَرُ النَّاسِ وَلَوْ حَرَصْتَ بِمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ [يُوسُفَ: ١٠٣] . وَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَإِنْ تُطِعْ أَكْثَرَ مَنْ فِي الأرْضِ يُضِلُّوكَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ﴾ [الْأَنْعَامِ: ١١٦] وَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَمَا يُؤْمِنُ أَكْثَرُهُمْ بِاللَّهِ إِلا وَهُمْ مُشْرِكُونَ﴾ [يُوسُفَ: ١٠٦] .

---

## 7:4-7 — verses 4-7 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says: {And how many a town have We destroyed} that is, because of their opposition to Our messengers and their denial of them, so that this was followed by disgrace in this world joined to humiliation in the Hereafter, just as the Almighty said: {And indeed, messengers were mocked before you, but that which they mocked was encompassed by those who scoffed at them} [al-An'am: 10]. And the Almighty said: {And how many a town have We destroyed while it was doing wrong, so it is fallen down upon its roofs, and how many a well abandoned and lofty palace} [al-Hajj: 45].

And the Almighty said: {And how many a town have We destroyed that exulted in its means of livelihood, and those are their dwellings, not inhabited after them except a little, and We were the inheritors} [al-Qasas: 58].

His saying: {Then Our punishment came to it by night or while they were sleeping at noon} that is, some of them had God's command, His punishment and His vengeance come to them {by night}, that is, at night, {or while they were sleeping at noon}, from al-qaylulah, which is the rest taken in the middle of the day. Both of these times are times of heedlessness and diversion, as the Almighty said: {Do the people of the towns feel secure that Our punishment will not come to them by night while they are asleep? Or do the people of the towns feel secure that Our punishment will not come to them in broad daylight while they are at play?} [al-A'raf: 97, 98]. And He said: {Do those who plot evil deeds feel secure that God will not cause the earth to swallow them or that the punishment will not come upon them from where they do not perceive? Or that He will not seize them in the midst of their going about, and they will not be able to escape? Or that He will not seize them gradually in a state of fear? Indeed your Lord is Most Kind, Most Merciful} [al-Nahl: 45-47].

His saying: {And their cry, when Our punishment came to them, was nothing but that they said: Indeed, we were wrongdoers} that is, their statement when the punishment came was nothing but that they confessed their sins and that they deserved this. As the Almighty said: {And how many a town We shattered that was doing wrong, and We raised up after it another people. Then when they perceived Our punishment, behold, they were fleeing from it. Do not flee, and return to that in which you were given luxury and to your dwellings, so that you may be questioned. They said: O woe to us, indeed we were wrongdoers. And that cry of theirs did not cease until We made them a reaped harvest,} extinguished [al-Anbiya: 11-15].

Ibn Jarir said: In this verse there is clear proof of the soundness of what has come in the report from the Messenger of God ﷺ, in his saying: "No people were destroyed until they had been given an excuse from within themselves." Ibn Humayd narrated this to us, [chain] Jarir, from Abu Sinan, from Abd al-Malik ibn Maysarah al-Zarrad, who said: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may God be pleased with him) said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "No people were destroyed until they had been given an excuse from within themselves." He said: I said to Abd al-Malik: How can that be? He said: Then he recited this verse: {And their cry, when Our punishment came to them, was nothing but that they said: Indeed, we were wrongdoers}.

His saying: {Then We will surely question those to whom [messengers] were sent} the verse, is like His saying: {And the Day He will call them and say: What did you answer the messengers?} [al-Qasas: 65], and His saying: {The Day God will gather the messengers and say: What was the response you received? They will say: We have no knowledge; indeed it is You who is the Knower of the unseen} [al-Ma'idah: 109]. So the Lord, blessed and exalted, on the Day of Resurrection questions the nations about how they responded to His messengers regarding what they were sent with, and He also questions the messengers about the conveying of His messages. This is why Ali ibn Abi Talhah, from Ibn Abbas, said in the exegesis of this verse: {Then We will surely question those to whom [messengers] were sent, and We will surely question the messengers}: God questions the people about how they responded to the messengers, and He questions the messengers about what they conveyed.

Ibn Mardawayh said: [chain] Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim, [chain] Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, [chain] Abu Sa'id al-Kindi, [chain] al-Muharibi, from Layth, from Nafi', from Ibn Umar (may God be pleased with them both), who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Each of you is a shepherd and each of you is responsible for his flock. The leader is questioned about the people, the man is questioned about his family, the woman is questioned about the household of her husband, and the slave is questioned about the property of his master." Layth said: Ibn Tawus narrated to me the same, then he recited: {Then We will surely question those to whom [messengers] were sent, and We will surely question the messengers}.

This hadith is recorded in the two Sahihs without this addition.

Ibn Abbas said regarding {Then We will surely relate to them with knowledge, and We were not absent}: The book will be placed on the Day of Resurrection, and it will speak of what they used to do. {And We were not absent} means that the Almighty informs His servants on the Day of Resurrection of what they said and what they did, whether little or much, great or small, because He, the Almighty, is a witness over everything, nothing is absent from Him, and He is heedless of nothing. Rather, He is the Knower of the treachery of the eyes and what the breasts conceal, {And not a leaf falls but He knows it, nor a grain in the darknesses of the earth, nor anything moist or dry, but that it is in a clear record} [al-An'am: 59].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَكَمْ مِنْ قَرْيَةٍ أَهْلَكْنَاهَا﴾ أَيْ: بِمُخَالَفَةِ رُسُلِنَا وَتَكْذِيبِهِمْ، فَأَعْقَبَهُمْ ذَلِكَ خِزْيُ الدُّنْيَا مَوْصُولًا بذُلِّ الْآخِرَةِ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَقَدِ اسْتُهْزِئَ بِرُسُلٍ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ فَحَاقَ بِالَّذِينَ سَخِرُوا مِنْهُمْ مَا كَانُوا بِهِ يَسْتَهْزِئُونَ﴾ [الْأَنْعَامِ: ١٠] . وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَكَأَيِّنْ مِنْ قَرْيَةٍ أَهْلَكْنَاهَا وَهِيَ ظَالِمَةٌ فَهِيَ خَاوِيَةٌ عَلَى عُرُوشِهَا وَبِئْرٍ مُعَطَّلَةٍ وَقَصْرٍ مَشِيدٍ﴾ [الحج: ٤٥] .

وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَكَمْ أَهْلَكْنَا مِنْ قَرْيَةٍ بَطِرَتْ مَعِيشَتَهَا فَتِلْكَ مَسَاكِنُهُمْ لَمْ تُسْكَنْ مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ إِلا قَلِيلا وَكُنَّا نَحْنُ الْوَارِثِينَ﴾ [الْقَصَصِ: ٥٨] .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَجَاءَهَا بَأْسُنَا بَيَاتًا أَوْ هُمْ قَائِلُونَ﴾ أَيْ: فَكَانَ مِنْهُمْ مَنْ جَاءَهُ أَمْرُ اللَّهِ وَبَأْسُهُ وَنِقْمَتُهُ ﴿بَيَاتًا﴾ أَيْ: لَيْلًا ﴿أَوْ هُمْ قَائِلُونَ﴾ مِنَ الْقَيْلُولَةِ، وَهِيَ: الِاسْتِرَاحَةُ وَسَطَ النَّهَارِ. وَكِلَا الْوَقْتَيْنِ وَقْتُ غَفْلة ولَهْو كَمَا قَالَ [تَعَالَى] ﴿أَفَأَمِنَ أَهْلُ الْقُرَى أَنْ يَأْتِيَهُمْ بَأْسُنَا بَيَاتًا وَهُمْ نَائِمُون * أَوَأَمِنَ أَهْلُ الْقُرَى أَنْ يَأْتِيَهُمْ بَأْسُنَا ضُحًى وَهُمْ يَلْعَبُونَ﴾ [الْأَعْرَافِ: ٩٧، ٩٨] . وَقَالَ: ﴿أَفَأَمِنَ الَّذِينَ مَكَرُوا السَّيِّئَاتِ أَنْ يَخْسِفَ اللَّهُ بِهِمُ الأرْضَ أَوْ يَأْتِيَهُمُ الْعَذَابُ مِنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَشْعُرُونَ * أَوْ يَأْخُذَهُمْ فِي تَقَلُّبِهِمْ فَمَا هُمْ بِمُعْجِزِين * أَوْ يَأْخُذَهُمْ عَلَى تَخَوُّفٍ فَإِنَّ رَبَّكُمْ لَرَءُوفٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ [النَّحْلِ: ٤٥-٤٧] .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَمَا كَانَ دَعْوَاهُمْ إِذْ جَاءَهُمْ بَأْسُنَا إِلا أَنْ قَالُوا إِنَّا كُنَّا ظَالِمِينَ﴾ أَيْ: فَمَا كَانَ قَوْلُهُمْ عِنْدَ مَجِيءِ الْعَذَابِ إِلَّا أَنِ اعْتَرَفُوا بِذُنُوبِهِمْ، وَأَنَّهُمْ حَقِيقُونَ بِهَذَا. كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَكَمْ قَصَمْنَا مِن قَرْيَةٍ كَانَتْ ظَالِمَةً [وَأَنْشَأَْ بَعْدَهَا قَوْمًا آخَرِينَ * فَلَمَّا أَحَسُّوا بَأْسَنَا إِذَا هُمْ مِنْهَا يَرْكُضُونَ * لَا تَرْكُضُوا وَارْجِعُوا إِلَى مَا أُتْرِفْتُمْ فِيهِ وَمَسَاكِنِكُمْ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُسْأَلُونَ. قَالُوا يَا وَيْلَنَا إِنَّا كُنَّا ظَالِمِينَ * فَمَا زَالَتْ تِلْكَ دَعْوَاهُمْ حَتَّى جَعَلْنَاهُمْ حَصِيدًا] خَامِدِين﴾ [الْأَنْبِيَاءِ: ١١-١٥] .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ الدَّلَالَةُ الْوَاضِحَةُ عَلَى صِحَّةِ مَا جَاءَتْ بِهِ الرِّوَايَةُ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ: "مَا هَلَكَ قَوْمٌ حَتَّى يُعْذِروا مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ"، حَدَّثَنَا بِذَلِكَ ابْنُ حُمَيْد، حَدَّثَنَا جَرِيرٌ، عَنْ أَبِي سِنان، عَنْ عَبْدِ الْمَلِكِ بْنِ مَيْسَرة الزَّرَّادِ قَالَ: قَالَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ [رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ] قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "مَا هَلَكَ قَوْمٌ حَتَّى يُعْذِروا مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ". قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِعَبْدِ الْمَلِكِ: كَيْفَ يَكُونُ ذَاكَ؟ قَالَ: فَقَرَأَ هَذِهِ الْآيَةَ: ﴿فَمَا كَانَ دَعْوَاهُمْ إِذْ جَاءَهُمْ بَأْسُنَا إِلا أَنْ قَالُوا إِنَّا كُنَّا ظَالِمِينَ﴾ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَلَنَسْأَلَنَّ الَّذِينَ أُرْسِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ الْآيَةَ، كَقَوْلِهِ [تَعَالَى] ﴿وَيَوْمَ يُنَادِيهِمْ فَيَقُولُ مَاذَا أَجَبْتُمُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ﴾ [الْقَصَصِ: ٦٥] وَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿يَوْمَ يَجْمَعُ اللَّهُ الرُّسُلَ فَيَقُولُ مَاذَا أُجِبْتُمْ قَالُوا لَا عِلْمَ لَنَا إِنَّكَ أَنْتَ عَلامُ الْغُيُوبِ﴾ [الْمَائِدَةِ: ١٠٩] فالرَّبُّ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ يَسْأَلُ الْأُمَمَ عَمَّا أَجَابُوا رُسُلَهُ فِيمَا أَرْسَلَهُمْ بِهِ، وَيَسْأَلُ الرُّسُلَ أَيْضًا عَنْ إِبْلَاغِ رِسَالَاتِهِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، فِي تَفْسِيرِ هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: ﴿فَلَنَسْأَلَنَّ الَّذِينَ أُرْسِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَلَنَسْأَلَنَّ الْمُرْسَلِينَ﴾ قَالَ: يَسْأَلُ اللَّهُ النَّاسَ عَمَّا أَجَابُوا الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَيَسْأَلُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ عَمَّا بَلَّغُوا.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ مَرْدُويه: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، حَدَّثَنَا إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ الْحَسَنِ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سَعِيدٍ الكنْدي، حَدَّثَنَا الْمُحَارِبِيُّ، عَنْ لَيْث، عَنْ نَافِعٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ [رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا] قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "كُلُّكُمْ رَاعٍ وَكُلُّكُمْ مَسْئُولٌ عَنْ رَعِيَّتِهِ، فالإمام يُسْأل عن الرجل وَالرَّجُلُ يُسْأَلُ عَنْ أَهْلِهِ وَالْمَرْأَةُ تُسْأَلُ عَنْ بَيْتِ زَوْجِهَا، وَالْعَبْدُ يُسْأَلُ عَنْ مَالِ سَيِّدِهِ". قَالَ اللَّيْثُ: وَحَدَّثَنِي ابْنُ طَاوُسٍ، مِثْلَهُ، ثُمَّ قَرَأَ: ﴿فَلَنَسْأَلَنَّ الَّذِينَ أُرْسِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَلَنَسْأَلَنَّ الْمُرْسَلِينَ﴾ .

وَهَذَا الْحَدِيثُ مُخَرَّجٌ فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ بِدُونِ هَذِهِ الزِّيَادَةِ 

وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿فَلَنَقُصَّنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ بِعِلْمٍ وَمَا كُنَّا غَائِبِينَ﴾ يُوضَعُ الْكِتَابُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ، فَيَتَكَلَّمُ بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ، ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا غَائِبِينَ﴾ يَعْنِي: أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى يُخْبِرُ عِبَادَهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ بِمَا قَالُوا وَبِمَا عَمِلُوا، مِنْ قَلِيلٍ وَكَثِيرٍ، وَجَلِيلٍ وحَقِير؛ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَالَى شَهِيدٌ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ، لَا يَغِيبُ عَنْهُ شَيْءٌ، وَلَا يَغْفَلُ عَنْ شَيْءٍ، بَلْ هُوَ الْعَالِمُ بِخَائِنَةِ الْأَعْيُنِ وَمَا تُخْفِي الصُّدُورُ، ﴿وَمَا تَسْقُطُ مِنْ وَرَقَةٍ إِلا يَعْلَمُهَا وَلا حَبَّةٍ فِي ظُلُمَاتِ الأرْضِ وَلا رَطْبٍ وَلا يَابِسٍ إِلا فِي كِتَابٍ مُبِينٍ﴾ [الْأَنْعَامِ: ٥٩] .

---

## 7:8-9 — verses 8-9 (shared commentary)

### Translation

He, [blessed and] exalted, says: {And the weighing}, that is, of the deeds on the Day of Resurrection, {is the truth}, that is, He, exalted, does not wrong anyone, as He, exalted, has said: {And We place the scales of justice for the Day of Resurrection, so that no soul will be wronged at all. Even if it be the weight of a mustard seed, We will bring it forth. And sufficient are We as Reckoner} [al-Anbiya: 47]. And He, exalted, said: {Indeed, Allah does not wrong even the weight of an atom, and if there is a good deed, He multiplies it and gives from Himself a great reward} [al-Nisa: 40]. And He, exalted, said: {Then as for one whose scales are heavy, he will be in a pleasant life. But as for one whose scales are light, his refuge will be an abyss. And what can make you know what it is? A blazing fire} [al-Qari'ah: 6-11]. And He, exalted, said: {So when the Horn is blown, there will be no relations among them that Day, nor will they ask about one another. Then those whose scales are heavy, it is they who are the successful. But those whose scales are light, it is they who have lost their souls, abiding forever in Hell} [al-Mu'minun: 101-103].

A section:

As for what is placed on the scale on the Day of Resurrection, it is said: it is the deeds, and although they are accidents (non-corporeal attributes), Allah, exalted, transforms them on the Day of Resurrection into bodies.

Al-Baghawi said: this is reported from Ibn Abbas, as has come in the authentic hadith that "al-Baqarah" and "Al Imran" will come on the Day of Resurrection as if they were two clouds, or two shades, or two flocks of birds flying in formation. Among such reports in the authentic hadith is the account of the Qur'an, that it comes to its companion in the form of a pale-faced young man, who says: who are you? And he replies: I am the Qur'an which kept your nights sleepless and your days thirsty (from fasting). And in the hadith of al-Bara, in the account of the questioning in the grave: "a young man of good complexion and pleasant fragrance comes to the believer and says: who are you? He replies: I am your righteous deed." And the opposite of this is mentioned regarding the disbeliever and the hypocrite.

And it is said: the record book of deeds is weighed, as has come in the hadith of the card (al-bitaqah), concerning the man who is brought forth and for whom ninety-nine scrolls are placed in one pan of the scale, each scroll stretching as far as the eye can see. Then that card is brought, on which is written: "There is no god but Allah." He says: O Lord, what is this card compared to these scrolls? Allah, exalted, says: you will not be wronged. So that card is placed in the pan of the scale. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "So the scrolls were outweighed, and the card was heavy."

Al-Tirmidhi related something similar to this and deemed it sound (sahih).

And it is said: the doer of the deed himself is weighed, as in the hadith: "A fat man will be brought on the Day of Resurrection, and he will not weigh with Allah so much as the wing of a mosquito." Then he recited: {So We will not establish for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight} [al-Kahf: 105].

And in the accounts of the merits of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Do you marvel at the thinness of his two shins? By the One in whose hand is my soul, they will be heavier on the scale than Mount Uhud."

It is possible to reconcile these reports by holding that all of them are correct: sometimes the deeds themselves are weighed, sometimes their vessels (the record books) are weighed, and sometimes the doer of the deed is weighed. And Allah knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يقول [تبارك و] تعالى: ﴿وَالْوَزْن﴾ أَيْ: لِلْأَعْمَالِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ ﴿الْحَق﴾ أَيْ: لَا يَظْلِمُ تَعَالَى أَحَدًا، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ لِيَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ فَلا تُظْلَمُ نَفْسٌ شَيْئًا وَإِنْ كَانَ مِثْقَالَ حَبَّةٍ مِنْ خَرْدَلٍ أَتَيْنَا بِهَا وَكَفَى بِنَا حَاسِبِينَ﴾ [الْأَنْبِيَاءِ: ٤٧] وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَظْلِمُ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ وَإِنْ تَكُ حَسَنَةً يُضَاعِفْهَا وَيُؤْتِ مِنْ لَدُنْهُ أَجْرًا عَظِيمًا﴾ [النِّسَاءِ: ٤٠] وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَأَمَّا مَنْ ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَهُوَ فِي عِيشَةٍ رَاضِيَةٍ * وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُمُّهُ هَاوِيَةٌ * وَمَا أَدْرَاكَ مَا هِيَهْ * نَارٌ حَامِيَةٌ﴾ [الْقَارِعَةِ: ٦-١١] وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَإِذَا نُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَلا أَنْسَابَ بَيْنَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ وَلا يَتَسَاءَلُونَ * فَمَنْ ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ * وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ فِي جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدُونَ﴾ [الْمُؤْمِنُونَ: ١٠١ -١٠٣] .

فَصْلٌ:

وَالَّذِي يُوضَعُ فِي الْمِيزَانِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ قِيلَ: الْأَعْمَالُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أَعْرَاضًا، إِلَّا أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى يَقْلِبُهَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ أَجْسَامًا.

قَالَ الْبَغَوِيُّ: يُرْوَى هَذَا عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ كَمَا جَاءَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ مِنْ أَنَّ "الْبَقَرَةَ" وَ "آلَ عِمْرَانَ" يَأْتِيَانِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ كَأَنَّهُمَا غَمَامَتَانِ -أَوْ: غيَايَتان -أَوْ فِرْقَان مِنْ طَيْرٍ صَوَافّ. مِنْ ذَلِكَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ قِصَّةُ الْقُرْآنِ وَأَنَّهُ يَأْتِي صَاحِبَهُ فِي صُورَةِ شَابٍّ شَاحِبِ اللَّون، فَيَقُولُ: مَنْ أَنْتَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: أَنَا الْقُرْآنُ الَّذِي أَسْهَرْتُ لَيْلَكَ وَأَظْمَأْتُ نَهَارَكَ وَفِي حَدِيثِ الْبَرَاءِ، فِي قِصَّةِ سُؤَالِ الْقَبْرِ: "فَيَأْتِي الْمُؤْمِنَ شابٌّ حَسَنُ اللَّوْنِ طَيِّبُ الرِّيحِ، فَيَقُولُ: مَنْ أَنْتَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: أَنَا عَمَلُكَ الصَّالِحُ" وَذَكَرَ عَكْسَهُ فِي شَأْنِ الْكَافِرِ وَالْمُنَافِقِ.

وَقِيلَ: يُوزَنُ كِتَابُ الْأَعْمَالِ، كَمَا جَاءَ فِي حَدِيثِ الْبِطَاقَةِ، فِي الرَّجُلِ الَّذِي يُؤْتَى بِهِ وَيُوضَعُ لَهُ فِي كِفَّة تِسْعَةٌ وَتِسْعُونَ سِجِلًّا كُلُّ سِجِلّ مَدّ الْبَصَرِ، ثُمَّ يُؤْتَى بِتِلْكَ الْبِطَاقَةِ فِيهَا: "لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ" فَيَقُولُ: يَا رَبِّ، وَمَا هَذِهِ الْبِطَاقَةُ مَعَ هَذِهِ السِّجِلَّاتِ؟ فَيَقُولُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: إِنَّكَ لَا تُظلَم. فَتُوضَعُ تِلْكَ الْبِطَاقَةُ فِي كِفَّةِ الْمِيزَانِ. قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "فَطاشَت السِّجِلَّاتُ، وثَقُلَتِ الْبِطَاقَةُ".

رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ بِنَحْوٍ مِنْ هَذَا وَصَحَّحَهُ.

وَقِيلَ: يُوزَنُ صَاحِبُ الْعَمَلِ، كَمَا فِي الْحَدِيثِ: "يُؤتَى يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ بِالرَّجُلِ السَّمِين، فَلَا يَزِن عِنْدَ اللَّهِ جَنَاح بَعُوضَة" ثُمَّ قَرَأَ: ﴿فَلا نُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزْنًا﴾ [الْكَهْفِ: ١٠٥] .

وَفِي مَنَاقِبِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: "أَتَعْجَبُونَ مِنْ دِقَّة ساقَيْهِ، فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَهُمَا فِي الْمِيزَانِ أَثْقَلُ مِنْ أُحُدٍ" 

وَقَدْ يُمْكِنُ الْجَمْعُ بَيْنَ هَذِهِ الْآثَارِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ ذَلِكَ كُلُّهُ صَحِيحًا، فَتَارَةً تُوزَنُ الْأَعْمَالُ، وَتَارَةً تُوزَنُ مَحَالُّهَا، وَتَارَةً يُوزَنُ فَاعِلُهَا، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

---

## 7:10 — verse 10

### Translation

The Exalted says, showing His favor to His servants regarding what He established for them: that He made the earth a place of settlement, and made for it firm mountains and rivers, and made for them upon it dwellings and houses, and made lawful its benefits, and subjected the clouds to their service so as to bring forth their provisions from it, and made for them upon it means of livelihood, that is, sources of earning and means by which they trade and pursue various kinds of livelihoods. Yet most of them, despite all this, show little gratitude for it, as the Exalted said: {And if you were to count the favor of Allah, you could not enumerate it. Indeed, man is truly unjust and ungrateful} [Ibrahim: 34].

All reciters read {ma'ayish} without a hamza, except Abd al-Rahman ibn Hurmuz al-A'raj, who pronounced it with a hamza. The correct reading, which the majority hold, is without a hamza, because ma'ayish is the plural of ma'ishah (livelihood), from 'asha ya'ishu 'ayshan (he lived, he lives, living). The original form of ma'ishah was "ma'yishah," but the kasrah on the ya was found heavy, so it was transferred to the 'ayn, becoming ma'ishah. When it was made plural, the vowel returned to the ya since the heaviness had been removed, and so it was said: ma'ayish. Its pattern is mafa'il, because the ya is an original letter within the word.

This differs from words like mada'in, saha'if, and basa'ir, the plurals of madinah, sahifah, and basirah, from madana, sahafa, and absara, in which the ya is an added letter. For this reason, they are pluralized on the pattern of fa'a'il, and are therefore pronounced with a hamza. And Allah knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُمْتَنًّا عَلَى عَبِيدِهِ فِيمَا مَكَّنَ لَهُمْ مِنْ أَنَّهُ جَعَل الْأَرْضَ قَرَارًا، وَجَعَلَ لَهَا رَوَاسِيَ وَأَنْهَارًا، وَجَعَلَ لَهُمْ فِيهَا مَنَازِلَ وَبُيُوتًا، وَأَبَاحَ مَنَافِعَهَا، وسَخَّر لَهُمُ السَّحَابَ لِإِخْرَاجِ أَرْزَاقِهِمْ مِنْهَا، وَجَعَلَ لَهُمْ فِيهَا مَعَايِشَ، أَيْ: مَكَاسِبَ وَأَسْبَابًا يَتَّجِرُونَ فِيهَا، وَيَتَسَبَّبُونَ أَنْوَاعَ الْأَسْبَابِ، وَأَكْثَرُهُمْ مَعَ هَذَا قَلِيلُ الشُّكْرِ عَلَى ذَلِكَ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَإِنْ تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَةَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا إِنَّ الإنْسَانَ لَظَلُومٌ كَفَّارٌ﴾ [إِبْرَاهِيمَ: ٣٤] .

وَقَدْ قَرَأَ الْجَمِيعُ: ﴿مَعَايِش﴾ بِلَا هَمْزٍ، إِلَّا عَبْدَ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنَ هُرْمُز الْأَعْرَجَ فَإِنَّهُ هَمَزَهَا. وَالصَّوَابُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُونَ بِلَا هَمْزٍ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعَايِشَ جَمْعُ مَعِيشَةٍ، مِنْ عَاشَ يَعِيشُ عَيْشًا، وَمَعِيشَةٌ أَصْلُهَا "مَعْيِشَة" فَاسْتُثْقِلَتِ الْكَسْرَةُ عَلَى الْيَاءِ، فَنُقِلَتْ إِلَى الْعَيْنِ فَصَارَتْ مَعِيشة، فَلَمَّا جُمِعَتْ رَجَعَتِ الْحَرَكَةُ إِلَى الْيَاءِ لِزَوَالِ الِاسْتِثْقَالِ، فَقِيلَ: مَعَايِشُ. وَوَزْنُهُ مَفَاعِلُ؛ لِأَنَّ الْيَاءَ أَصْلِيَّةٌ فِي الكلمة. بخلاف مدائن وَصَحَائِفَ وَبَصَائِرَ، جَمْعِ مَدِينَةٍ وَصَحِيفَةٍ وَبَصِيرَةٍ مِنْ: مَدَنَ وَصَحَفَ وَأَبْصَرَ، فَإِنَّ الْيَاءَ فِيهَا زَائِدَةٌ، وَلِهَذَا تُجْمَعُ عَلَى فَعَائِلَ، وَتُهْمَزُ لِذَلِكَ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

---

## 7:11 — verse 11

### Translation

Allah, exalted is He, alerts the children of Adam in this passage to the nobility of their father Adam, and makes clear to them the enmity of their enemy Iblis, and what he harbors of envy toward them and toward their father Adam, so that they may be wary of him and not follow his paths. He, exalted is He, said: {And We have certainly created you, then We fashioned you, then We said to the angels, "Prostrate to Adam" [so they prostrated]}. This is like His saying, exalted is He: {And when your Lord said to the angels, "Indeed I am going to create a human being from clay, from an altered black mud. So when I have proportioned him and breathed into him of My spirit, then fall down to him in prostration" [so the angels prostrated]} to the end of the verse [al-Hijr: 28-30]. This is because when He, exalted is He, created Adam, peace be upon him, with His hand from sticky clay, and fashioned him into a well-proportioned human being, and breathed into him of His spirit, and commanded the angels to prostrate to him in exaltation of the majesty and glory of the Lord, exalted is He, they all heard and obeyed, except Iblis, who was not among those who prostrated. Discussion of Iblis has already preceded at the beginning of the tafsir of "Surat al-Baqarah."

What we have established here is the choice of Ibn Jarir: that what is meant by all of this is Adam, peace be upon him.

Sufyan al-Thawri said, from al-A'mash, from al-Minhal ibn Amr, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas, regarding {And We have certainly created you, then We fashioned you}: he said, they were created in the loins of men, and fashioned in the wombs of women.

Al-Hakim narrated it, and said: sahih (authentic) according to the criterion of the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim), though they did not extract it.

Ibn Jarir also transmitted from some of the salaf (early generations) that what is meant by "We created you, then We fashioned you" is the offspring.

Al-Rabi' ibn Anas, al-Suddi, Qatadah, and al-Dahhak said regarding this verse, {And We have certainly created you, then We fashioned you}: meaning, We created Adam, then We fashioned his offspring.

There is something questionable in this, because He said after it: {then We said to the angels, "Prostrate to Adam"}, which indicates that what is meant by that is Adam himself. It was only expressed in the plural because he is the father of mankind, just as Allah, exalted is He, says to the Children of Israel who were living in the time of the Messenger ﷺ: {And We shaded you with clouds and sent down upon you manna and quails} [al-Baqarah: 57], while what is actually meant are their forefathers who lived in the time of Moses, peace be upon him. But since that favor was bestowed upon the forefathers who are the origin, it came to be as though it applied to the descendants as well. This differs from His saying, exalted is He: {And We did certainly create man from an extract of clay, [then We made him a sperm-drop in a firm lodging]} [al-Mu'minun: 12-13], for what is meant by it is Adam, who was created from the extract, while his offspring are created from a sperm-drop. This is valid because what is meant by "We created man" is the species, not a specific individual, and Allah knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُنَبِّهُ تَعَالَى بَنِي آدَمَ فِي هَذَا الْمَقَامِ عَلَى شَرَفِ أَبِيهِمْ آدَمَ، وَيُبَيِّنُ لَهُمْ عَدَاوَةَ عَدُوِّهِمْ إِبْلِيسَ، وَمَا هُوَ مُنْطَوٍ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الْحَسَدِ لَهُمْ وَلِأَبِيهِمْ آدَمَ، لِيَحْذَرُوهُ وَلَا يَتَّبِعُوا طَرَائِقَهُ، فَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلائِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لآدَمَ [فَسَجَدُوا] ﴾ وَهَذَا كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَإِذْ قَالَ رَبُّكَ لِلْمَلائِكَةِ إِنِّي خَالِقٌ بَشَرًا مِنْ صَلْصَالٍ مِنْ حَمَإٍ مَسْنُونٍ فَإِذَا سَوَّيْتُهُ وَنَفَخْتُ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِي فَقَعُوا لَهُ سَاجِدِينَ [فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ] ﴾ الْآيَةَ [الْحِجْرِ: ٢٨ -٣٠] ، وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ تَعَالَى لَمَّا خَلَقَ آدَمَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، بِيَدِهِ مِنْ طِينٍ لَازِبٍ، وَصَوَّرَهُ بَشَرًا [سَوِيًّا] وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِهِ، وَأَمَرَ الْمَلَائِكَةَ بِالسُّجُودِ لَهُ تَعْظِيمًا لِشَأْنِ الرَّبِّ تَعَالَى وَجَلَالِهِ، فَسَمِعُوا كُلُّهُمْ وَأَطَاعُوا، إِلَّا إِبْلِيسَ لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنَ السَّاجِدِينَ. وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ الْكَلَامُ عَلَى إِبْلِيسَ فِي أَوَّلِ تَفْسِيرِ "سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ".

وَهَذَا الَّذِي قَرَّرْنَاهُ هُوَ اخْتِيَارُ ابْنِ جَرِيرٍ: أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ آدَمُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ.

وَقَالَ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنِ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنِ المِنْهَال بْنِ عَمْرٍو، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْر، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَاكُمْ﴾ قَالَ: خُلِقوا فِي أَصْلَابِ الرِّجَالِ، وصُوِّروا فِي أَرْحَامِ النِّسَاءِ.

رَوَاهُ الْحَاكِمُ، وَقَالَ: صَحِيحٌ عَلَى شَرْطِ الشَّيْخَيْنِ، وَلَمْ يُخَرِّجَاهُ 

وَنَقَلَهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ عَنْ بَعْضِ السَّلَفِ أَيْضًا: أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِخَلَقْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَاكُمِ: الذُّرِّيَّةُ.

وَقَالَ الرَّبِيعُ بْنُ أَنَسٍ، والسُّدي، وَقَتَادَةُ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: ﴿وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَاكُمْ﴾ أَيْ: خَلَقْنَا آدَمَ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَا الذُّرِّيَّةَ.

وَهَذَا فِيهِ نَظَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ بَعْدَهُ: ﴿ثُمَّ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلائِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لآدَمَ﴾ فَدَلَّ عَلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِذَلِكَ آدَمُ، وَإِنَّمَا قِيلَ ذَلِكَ بِالْجَمْعِ لِأَنَّهُ أَبُو الْبَشَرِ، كَمَا يَقُولُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى لِبَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ الَّذِينَ كَانُوا فِي زَمَنِ الرَّسُولِ ﷺ: ﴿وَظَلَّلْنَا عَلَيْكُمُ الْغَمَامَ وَأَنزلْنَا عَلَيْكُمُ الْمَنَّ وَالسَّلْوَى﴾ [الْبَقَرَةِ: ٥٧] وَالْمُرَادُ: آبَاؤُهُمُ الَّذِينَ كَانُوا فِي زَمَنِ مُوسَى [عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ] وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا كَانَ ذَلِكَ مِنَّةً عَلَى الْآبَاءِ الَّذِينَ هُمْ أصلٌ صَارَ كَأَنَّهُ وَاقِعٌ عَلَى الْأَبْنَاءِ. وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا الإنْسَانَ مِنْ سُلالَةٍ مِنْ طِينٍ [ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَاهُ نُطْفَةً فِي قَرَارٍ مَكِينٍ] ﴾ [الْمُؤْمِنُونَ: ١٢ -١٣] فَإِنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْهُ آدَمُ الْمَخْلُوقُ مِنَ السُّلَالَةِ وَذُرِّيَّتُهُ مخلوقون من نُطْفَةٍ، وَصَحَّ هَذَا لِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْ خَلَقْنَا الإنسان الجنس، لا معينا، والله أعلم.

---

## 7:12 — verse 12

### Translation

Some grammarians, in explaining the meaning of His saying, exalted is He, {What prevented you from prostrating when I commanded you}, said that "la" (no) here is superfluous.

Others said: it was added to reinforce the negation, as in the poet's saying:

"Ma in ra'aytu wa la sami'tu bi-mithlihi" (I never saw nor heard the like of it)

He introduced "in," which is a negation particle, upon "ma," which is also negating, in order to reinforce the negation. They said: likewise here, {What prevented you from prostrating}, given the preceding statement, {he was not among those who prostrated}.

Ibn Jarir related both of these views and rejected them, choosing instead the view that "prevented you" implies the meaning of another verb, its sense being: what made you need, obliged you, and compelled you not to prostrate when I commanded you, or something similar. This view is strong and good, and God knows best.

Iblis's statement, may God curse him, {I am better than him}, is an excuse greater than the sin itself. It is as though he refused obedience on the grounds that the more excellent one is not commanded to prostrate to the less excellent one. That is to say, may God curse him, meant: I am better than him, so how can You command me to prostrate to him? Then he explained why he was better than him: that he was created from fire, and fire is nobler than what You created him from, namely clay. So the accursed one looked only at the origin of the substance and did not look at the great honor bestowed, namely that God, exalted is He, created Adam with His own hand and breathed into him of His spirit. He made a corrupt analogy in opposition to the explicit text of His saying, exalted is He, {then fall down before him in prostration} [Sad: 72]. Thus he stood apart from among the angels by refusing to prostrate. For this he was "ablasa" from mercy, meaning he despaired of mercy. He erred, may God disfigure him, in his analogy and in his claim that fire is nobler than clay as well. For clay's nature is characterized by weightiness, forbearance, deliberateness, and steadiness, and clay is the locus of growth, increase, augmentation, and improvement. Fire's nature, on the other hand, is characterized by burning, rashness, and haste. For this reason his own element betrayed Iblis, while Adam's element benefited him in returning, repenting, submitting, yielding, and surrendering to God's command, in acknowledging his fault, and in seeking repentance and forgiveness.

In Sahih Muslim, from Aisha, may God be pleased with her, she said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "The angels were created from light, Iblis was created from a smokeless flame of fire, and Adam was created from that which has been described to you." Thus Muslim related it.

Ibn Mardawayh said: [chain] Aisha said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "God created the angels from the light of the Throne, and created the jinn from a [smokeless flame of] fire, and Adam was created from that which has been described to you." I said to Nu'aym ibn Hammad: Where did you hear this from Abd al-Razzaq? He said: In Yemen. And in some wordings of this hadith, outside the two Sahihs, it is stated: "and the wide-eyed houris were created from saffron."

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] al-Hasan, regarding His saying, {You created me from fire and created him from clay}, said: Iblis made an analogy, and he was the first to make an analogy. Its chain is sound.

He also said: [chain] Ibn Sirin said: The first to make an analogy was Iblis, and the sun and moon were only worshipped because of analogies. This chain is also sound.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ بَعْضُ النُّحَاةِ فِي تَوْجِيهِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿مَا [مَنَعَكَ] أَلا تَسْجُدَ إِذْ أَمَرْتُكَ﴾ لَا هَاهُنَا زَائِدَةٌ.

وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: زِيدَتْ لِتَأْكِيدِ الْجَحْدِ، كَقَوْلِ الشَّاعِرِ:

مَا إِنْ رأيتُ وَلَا سمعتُ بِمِثْلِهِ

فَأَدْخَلَ "إِنْ" وَهِيَ لِلنَّفْيِ، عَلَى "مَا" النَّافِيَةِ؛ لِتَأْكِيدِ النَّفْيِ، قَالُوا: وَكَذَلِكَ هَاهُنَا: ﴿مَا مَنَعَكَ أَلا تَسْجُدَ﴾ مَعَ تَقَدُّمِ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنَ السَّاجِدِينَ﴾

حَكَاهُمَا ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ وَرَدَّهُمَا، وَاخْتَارَ أَنَّ "مَنَعَكَ" تَضَمَّنَ مَعْنَى فِعْلٍ آخَرَ تَقْدِيرُهُ: مَا أَحْوَجَكَ وَأَلْزَمَكَ وَاضْطَرَّكَ أَلَّا تَسْجُدَ إِذْ أَمَرْتُكَ، وَنَحْوُ ذَلِكَ. وَهَذَا الْقَوْلُ قَوِيٌّ حَسَنٌ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَوْلُ إِبْلِيسَ لَعَنَهُ اللَّهُ: ﴿أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ﴾ مِنَ الْعُذْرِ الَّذِي هُوَ أَكْبَرُ مِنَ الذَّنْبِ، كَأَنَّهُ امْتَنَعَ مِنَ الطَّاعَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُؤْمَرُ الْفَاضِلُ بِالسُّجُودِ لِلْمَفْضُولِ، يَعْنِي لَعَنَهُ اللَّهُ: وَأَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ، فَكَيْفَ تَأْمُرُنِي بِالسُّجُودِ لَهُ؟ ثُمَّ بَيَّنَ أَنَّهُ خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ، بِأَنَّهُ خُلِقَ مِنْ نَارٍ، وَالنَّارُ أَشْرَفُ مِمَّا خَلَقْتَهُ مِنْهُ، وَهُوَ الطِّينُ، فَنَظَرَ اللَّعِينُ إِلَى أَصْلِ الْعُنْصُرِ، وَلَمْ يَنْظُرْ إِلَى التَّشْرِيفِ الْعَظِيمِ، وَهُوَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى خَلَقَ آدَمَ بِيَدِهِ، وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِهِ، وَقَاسَ قِيَاسًا فَاسِدًا فِي مُقَابَلَةِ نَصِّ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَقَعُوا لَهُ سَاجِدِينَ﴾ [ص:٧٢] فَشَذَّ مِنْ بَيْنِ الْمَلَائِكَةِ بتَرْك السُّجُودِ؛ فَلِهَذَا أَبْلَسَ مِنَ الرَّحْمَةِ، أَيْ: أَيِسَ مِنَ الرَّحْمَةِ، فَأَخْطَأَ قَبَّحه اللَّهُ فِي قِيَاسِهِ وَدَعْوَاهُ أَنَّ النَّارَ أَشْرَفُ مِنَ الطِّينِ أَيْضًا، فَإِنَّ الطِّينَ مِنْ شَأْنِهِ الرَّزَانَةُ وَالْحِلْمُ وَالْأَنَاةُ وَالتَّثَبُّتُ، وَالطِّينُ مَحَلُّ النَّبَاتِ وَالنُّمُوِّ وَالزِّيَادَةِ وَالْإِصْلَاحِ. وَالنَّارُ مِنْ شَأْنِهَا الْإِحْرَاقُ وَالطَّيْشُ وَالسُّرْعَةُ؛ وَلِهَذَا خَانَ إِبْلِيسَ عُنْصُرُهُ، وَنَفَعَ آدَمَ عُنْصُرُهُ فِي الرُّجُوعِ وَالْإِنَابَةِ وَالِاسْتِكَانَةِ وَالِانْقِيَادِ وَالِاسْتِسْلَامِ لِأَمْرِ اللَّهِ، وَالِاعْتِرَافِ وَطَلَبِ التَّوْبَةِ وَالْمَغْفِرَةِ.

وَفِي صَحِيحِ مُسْلِمٍ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "خُلِقَت الْمَلَائِكَةُ مِنْ نُورٍ، وخُلقَ إِبْلِيسُ مِنْ مَارِجٍ مِنْ نَارٍ، وَخُلِقَ آدَمُ مِمَّا وُصِفَ لَكُمْ" هَكَذَا رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ مَرْدُوَيه: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ جَعْفَرٍ، حَدَّثَنَا إِسْمَاعِيلُ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، حدثنا نُعَيم ابن حَمَّادٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ مَعْمَر، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ عُرْوَة، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "خَلَقَ اللَّهُ الْمَلَائِكَةَ مِنْ نُورِ الْعَرْشِ، وَخَلَقَ الْجَانَّ مِنْ [مَارِجٍ مِنْ] نَارٍ، وَخُلِقَ آدم مِمَّا وُصِفَ لَكُمْ". قُلْتُ لِنُعَيْمِ بْنِ حَمَّادٍ: أَيْنَ سَمِعْتَ هَذَا مِنْ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ؟ قَالَ: بِالْيَمَنِ وَفِي بَعْضِ أَلْفَاظِ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ فِي غَيْرِ الصَّحِيحِ: "وَخُلِقَتِ الْحُورُ الْعِينُ مِنَ الزَّعْفَرَانِ" .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا الْقَاسِمُ، حَدَّثَنَا الْحُسَيْنُ، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ كَثِيرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ شَوْذَب، عَنْ مَطَرٍ الوَرَّاق، عَنِ الْحَسَنِ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿خَلَقْتَنِي مِنْ نَارٍ وَخَلَقْتَهُ مِنْ طِينٍ﴾ قَالَ: قَاسَ إِبْلِيسُ، وَهُوَ أَوَّلُ مَنْ قَاسَ. إِسْنَادُهُ صَحِيحٌ.

وَقَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي عَمْرُو بْنُ مَالِكٍ، حَدَّثَنِي يَحْيَى بْنُ سُلَيْمٍ الطَّائِفِيُّ عَنْ هِشَامٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ قَالَ: أَوَّلُ مَنْ قَاسَ إِبْلِيسُ، وَمَا عُبِدت الشَّمْسُ وَالْقَمَرُ إِلَّا بِالْمَقَايِيسِ إِسْنَادٌ صَحِيحٌ أَيْضًا.

---

## 7:13-15 — verses 13-15 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says, addressing Iblis with a decree of predestined cosmic command: {So descend from it}, meaning: because of your disobedience to My command and your departure from obedience to Me, it is not fitting for you to be arrogant within it.

Many of the exegetes said: the pronoun refers back to Paradise, though it is also possible that it refers back to the rank he occupied in the highest heavenly dominion (al-malakut al-a'la).

{So go out, for indeed you are among the humiliated ones}, meaning: the abased, the contemptible ones. This was a treatment of him with the opposite of what he sought, a recompense for his intention with its very opposite. At that point, the accursed one sought a way out and asked for respite until the Day of Judgment. He said: {Grant me respite until the day they are resurrected. He said: indeed you are among those granted respite}. The Almighty granted him what he asked, on account of the wisdom, will, and decree that belong to Him, which cannot be opposed or resisted. There is no one who can override His judgment, and He is swift in reckoning.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُخَاطِبًا لِإِبْلِيسَ بِأَمْرٍ قَدَرِيٍّ كَوْنِيٍّ: ﴿فَاهْبِطْ مِنْهَا﴾ أَيْ: بِسَبَبِ عِصْيَانِكَ لِأَمْرِي، وَخُرُوجِكَ عَنْ طَاعَتِي، فَمَا يَكُونُ لَكَ أَنْ تَتَكَبَّرَ فِيهَا.

قَالَ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ الْمُفَسِّرِينَ: الضَّمِيرُ عَائِدٌ إِلَى الْجَنَّةِ، وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَائِدًا إِلَى الْمَنْزِلَةِ الَّتِي هُوَ فِيهَا فِي الْمَلَكُوتِ الْأَعْلَى.

﴿فَاخْرُجْ إِنَّكَ مِنَ الصَّاغِرِينَ﴾ أَيِ: الذَّلِيلِينَ الْحَقِيرِينَ، مُعَامَلَةً لَهُ بِنَقِيضِ قَصْدِهِ، مُكَافَأَةً لِمُرَادِهِ بِضِدِّهِ، فَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ اسْتَدْرَكَ اللَّعِينُ وَسَأَلَ النَّظْرَةَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، قَالَ: ﴿أَنْظِرْنِي إِلَى يَوْمِ يُبْعَثُونَ قَالَ إِنَّكَ مِنَ الْمُنْظَرِين﴾ أَجَابَهُ تَعَالَى إِلَى مَا سَأَلَ، لِمَا لَهُ فِي ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالْإِرَادَةِ وَالْمَشِيئَةِ الَّتِي لَا تُخَالَفُ وَلَا تُمَانَعُ، وَلَا مُعَقِّبَ لِحُكْمِهِ، وَهُوَ سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ.

---

## 7:16-17 — verses 16-17 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty informs that when Iblis was granted respite {until the day they are resurrected} and had secured that assurance for himself, he proceeded into obstinacy and rebellion, saying: {"Because You have led me astray, I will surely sit in wait for them on Your straight path"}, that is: just as You led me astray.

Ibn Abbas said: just as You caused me to go astray. Others said: just as You destroyed me, I will surely sit in wait for Your servants, whom You will create from the offspring of this one because of whom You have distanced me, upon {Your straight path}, that is, the path of truth and the way of salvation, and I will surely lead them astray from it so that they will not worship You and will not affirm Your oneness, because of Your having led me astray.

Some grammarians said that the "ba" here is an oath particle, as though he were saying: by Your leading me astray, I will surely sit in wait for them on Your straight path.

Mujahid said: {Your straight path} means: the truth.

Muhammad ibn Suqah reported from Awn ibn Abdullah: it means the road to Mecca.

Ibn Jarir said: the correct view is that the straight path is more general than all of that.

I say: this is because of what Imam Ahmad reported:

[chain] Hashim ibn al-Qasim, from Abu Aqil, that is Abdullah ibn Aqil al-Thaqafi, from Musa ibn al-Musayyab, from Salim ibn Abi al-Ja'd, from Sabrah ibn Abi Fakih, who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: "Indeed Satan sat in wait for the son of Adam along his paths. He sat in wait for him on the path of Islam and said: 'Will you submit and abandon your religion and the religion of your forefathers?' " He said: "So he disobeyed him and submitted." He said: "Then he sat in wait for him on the path of migration (hijrah) and said: 'Will you migrate and leave your land and your sky? The example of the migrant is like a horse tied on a tether.' So he disobeyed him and migrated. Then he sat in wait for him on the path of jihad, which is the striving of the self and of wealth, and said: 'Will you fight and be killed, so that your wife is married to another and your wealth is divided up?' " He said: "So he disobeyed him and strove." The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever among them does that and dies, it becomes a due right upon Allah that He admit him into Paradise. Or if he is killed, it becomes a due right upon Allah, Mighty and Majestic, that He admit him into Paradise. And if he drowns, it becomes a due right upon Allah that He admit him into Paradise. Or if a mount throws him and breaks his neck, it becomes a due right upon Allah that He admit him into Paradise."

Regarding His saying: {Then I will surely come to them from before them and from behind them, and from their right and from their left, and You will not find most of them grateful}, Ali ibn Abi Talhah reported from Ibn Abbas: {Then I will surely come to them from before them} means, I will cast doubt upon them regarding their afterlife; {and from behind them} means, I will make them desirous of their worldly life; {and from their right} means, I will make ambiguous to them the matter of their religion; {and from their left} means, I will make sins appealing to them.

Ali ibn Talhah said, in another report, and al-Awfi, both from Ibn Abbas: as for {from before them}, it refers to the side of their worldly life, and as for {from behind them}, it is the matter of their afterlife, and as for {from their right}, it is the side of their good deeds, and as for {from their left}, it is the side of their evil deeds.

Sa'id ibn Abi Arubah reported from Qatadah: he comes to them {from before them} and tells them that there is no resurrection, no Paradise, and no Fire; {and from behind them}, regarding the matter of the world, he adorns it for them and calls them to it; {and from their right}, regarding their good deeds, he holds them back from it; {and from their left}, he adorns evil deeds and sins for them, calls them to them, and commands them to do them. He comes to you, O son of Adam, from every direction, except that he does not come to you from above you, for he is not able to come between you and the mercy of Allah.

The same has been reported from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Hakam ibn Utaybah, al-Suddi, and Ibn Jarir, except that they said: {from before them} refers to the world, and {from behind them} refers to the afterlife.

Mujahid said: "from before them and from their right" means where they can see, and "from behind them and from their left" means where they cannot see.

Ibn Jarir preferred the view that what is meant is all the paths of good and evil: he obstructs them from the good, and makes evil beloved to them.

Al-Hakam ibn Aban reported from Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas, regarding His saying {Then I will surely come to them from before them and from behind them, and from their right and from their left}, that He did not say "from above them," because mercy descends from above them.

Ali ibn Abi Talhah reported from Ibn Abbas: {and You will not find most of them grateful}, he said: meaning those who affirm Your oneness.

This statement of Iblis is only his own supposition and conjecture, and in this he happened to match what actually occurred, as the Almighty said: {And indeed Iblis's assumption about them proved true, and they followed him, except for a party of the believers. And he had no authority over them, except that We might make known who believes in the Hereafter from who is in doubt about it. And your Lord is watchful over all things} [Saba: 20-21].

For this reason it has been reported in the hadith that one should seek refuge from Satan's domination over the human being from all of his directions, as the memorizer Abu Bakr al-Bazzar said in his Musnad:

[chain] Nasr ibn Ali, from Amr ibn Mujammi', from Yunus ibn Khabbab, from Ibn Jubayr ibn Mut'im, that is Nafi' ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas, and also [chain] Umar ibn al-Khattab al-Sijistani, from Abdullah ibn Ja'far, from Ubaydullah ibn Amr, from Zayd ibn Abi Unaysah, from Yunus ibn Khabbab, from Ibn Jubayr ibn Mut'im, from Ibn Abbas, who said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to say: "O Allah, I ask You for pardon and well-being in my religion and my worldly life, and my family and my wealth. O Allah, conceal my private faults, grant safety to my alarm, and protect me from before me and from behind me, and from my right and from my left, and from above me. And I seek refuge with You, O Allah, from being taken unawares from beneath me." Al-Bazzar related this alone and deemed it hasan (good).

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Waki', from Ubadah ibn Muslim al-Fazari, from Jubayr ibn Abi Sulayman ibn Jubayr ibn Mut'im, who said: I heard Abdullah ibn Umar say: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ never failed to make these supplications when morning came and when evening came: "O Allah, I ask You for well-being in this world and the next. O Allah, I ask You for pardon and well-being in my religion and my worldly life, and my family and my wealth. O Allah, conceal my private faults, and grant safety to my alarms. O Allah, protect me from before me and from behind me, and from my right and from my left, and from above me. And I seek refuge in Your greatness from being taken unawares from beneath me." Waki' said: meaning, being swallowed up by the earth.

It was also related by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim, from the hadith of Ubadah ibn Muslim, with the same wording, and al-Hakim said: its chain is sound (sahih).

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ لَمَّا أُنْظِرَ إِبْلِيسُ ﴿إِلَى يَوْمِ يُبْعَثُونَ﴾ وَاسْتَوْثَقَ إِبْلِيسُ بِذَلِكَ، أَخَذَ فِي الْمُعَانَدَةِ وَالتَّمَرُّدِ، فَقَالَ: ﴿فَبِمَا أَغْوَيْتَنِي لأقْعُدَنَّ لَهُمْ صِرَاطَكَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ﴾ أَيْ: كَمَا أَغْوَيْتَنِي.

قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: كَمَا أَضْلَلْتَنِي. وَقَالَ غَيْرُهُ: كَمَا أَهْلَكْتَنِي لَأَقْعُدَنَّ لِعِبَادِكَ -الَّذِينَ تخلقهم من ذُرِّيَّةِ هَذَا الَّذِي أَبْعَدْتَنِي بِسَبَبِهِ -عَلَى ﴿صِرَاطَكَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ﴾ أَيْ: طَرِيقَ الْحَقِّ وَسَبِيلَ النَّجَاةِ، وَلَأُضِلَّنَّهُمْ عَنْهَا لِئَلَّا يَعْبُدُوكَ وَلَا يُوَحِّدُوكَ بِسَبَبِ إِضْلَالِكَ إِيَّايَ.

وَقَالَ بَعْضُ النُّحَاةِ: الْبَاءُ هَاهُنَا قَسَمِيَّةٌ، كَأَنَّهُ يَقُولُ: فَبِإِغْوَائِكَ إِيَّايَ لَأَقْعُدَنَّ لَهُمْ صِرَاطَكَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ.

قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿صِرَاطَكَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ﴾ يَعْنِي: الْحَقَّ.

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ سُوقَةَ، عَنْ عَوْنِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ: يَعْنِي طَرِيقَ مَكَّةَ.

قَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: وَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّ الصِّرَاطَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ أَعَمُّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ [كُلِّهِ] .

قُلْتُ: لِمَا رَوَى الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ:

حَدَّثَنَا هَاشِمُ بْنُ الْقَاسِمِ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَقِيل-يَعْنِي الثَّقَفِيَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عَقِيلٍ -حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ الْمُسَيَّبِ، أَخْبَرَنِي سَالِمُ بْنُ أَبِي الجَعْد عَنْ سَبْرَة بْنِ أَبِي فَاكِه قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم يَقُولُ: "إِنَّ الشَّيْطَانَ قَعَدَ لِابْنِ آدَمَ بِطُرُقِهِ، فَقَعَدَ لَهُ بِطَرِيقِ الْإِسْلَامِ، فَقَالَ: أَتُسْلِمُ وَتَذَرُ دِينَكَ وَدِينَ آبَائِكَ؟ ". قَالَ: "فَعَصَاهُ وَأَسْلَمَ". قَالَ: "وَقَعَدَ لَهُ بِطَرِيقِ الْهِجْرَةِ فَقَالَ: أَتُهَاجِرُ وَتَدَعُ أَرْضَكَ وَسَمَاءَكَ، وَإِنَّمَا مَثَلُ الْمُهَاجِرِ كَالْفَرَسِ فِي الطّوَل؟ فَعَصَاهُ وَهَاجَرَ، ثُمَّ قَعَدَ لَهُ بِطَرِيقِ الْجِهَادِ، وَهُوَ جِهَادُ النَّفْسِ وَالْمَالِ، فَقَالَ: تُقَاتِلُ فَتُقْتَلُ، فَتُنْكَحُ الْمَرْأَةُ وَيُقَسَّمُ الْمَالُ؟ ". قَالَ: "فَعَصَاهُ، فَجَاهَدَ". قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "فَمَنْ فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ مِنْهُمْ فَمَاتَ، كَانَ حَقًّا عَلَى اللَّهِ أَنْ يُدْخِلَهُ الْجَنَّةَ، أَوْ قُتِلَ كَانَ حَقًّا عَلَى اللَّهِ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، أَنْ يُدْخِلَهُ الْجَنَّةَ، وَإِنْ غَرِقَ كَانَ حَقًّا عَلَى اللَّهِ أَنْ يُدْخِلَهُ الْجَنَّةَ، أَوْ وَقَصته دَابَّةٌ كَانَ حَقًّا عَلَى اللَّهِ أَنْ يَدْخُلَهُ الْجَنَّةَ" .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿ثمَُ لآتِيَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ [وَعَنْ أَيْمَانِهِمْ وِعَنْ شَمَائِلِهِمْ وَلا تَجِدُ أَكْثَرَهُمْ شَاكِرِينَ] ﴾ قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿ثُمَّ لآتِيَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ﴾ أُشَكِّكُهُمْ فِي آخِرَتِهِمْ، ﴿وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ﴾ أُرَغِّبُهُمْ فِي دُنْيَاهُمْ ﴿وَعَنْ أَيْمَانِهِمْ﴾ أشبَه عَلَيْهِمْ أَمْرَ دِينِهِمْ ﴿وَعَنْ شَمَائِلِهِمْ﴾ أُشَهِّي لَهُمُ الْمَعَاصِي.

وَقَالَ [عَلِيُّ] بْنُ طَلْحَةَ -فِي رِوَايَةٍ -والعَوْفي، كِلَاهُمَا عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: أَمَّا ﴿مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ﴾ فَمِنْ قِبَلِ دُنْيَاهُمْ، وَأَمَّا ﴿مِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ﴾ فَأَمْرُ آخِرَتِهِمْ، وَأَمَّا ﴿عَنْ أَيْمَانِهِمْ﴾ فَمِنْ قِبَل حَسَنَاتِهِمْ، وَأَمَّا ﴿عَنْ شَمَائِلِهِمْ﴾ فَمِنْ قِبَلِ سَيِّئَاتِهِمْ.

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ أَبِي عَرُوبَة، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ: أَتَاهُمْ ﴿مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ﴾ فَأَخْبَرَهُمْ أَنَّهُ لَا بعث ولا جَنَّةَ وَلَا نَارَ ﴿وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ﴾ مِنْ أَمْرِ الدُّنْيَا فزيَّنها لَهُمْ وَدَعَاهُمْ إِلَيْهَا وَ ﴿عَنْ أَيْمَانِهِم﴾ مِنْ قِبَلِ حَسَنَاتِهِمْ بَطَّاهم عَنْهَا ﴿وَعَنْ شَمَائِلِهِمْ﴾ زَيَّنَ لَهُمُ السَّيِّئَاتِ وَالْمَعَاصِيَ، وَدَعَاهُمْ إِلَيْهَا، وَأَمَرَهُمْ بِهَا. أَتَاكَ يَا ابْنَ آدَمَ مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهٍ، غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَأْتِكَ مِنْ فَوْقِكَ، لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ أَنْ يَحُولَ بَيْنَكَ وَبَيْنَ رَحْمَةِ اللَّهِ.

وَكَذَا رُوي عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعي، وَالْحَكَمِ بْنِ عُتَيْبَةَ وَالسُّدِّيِّ، وَابْنِ جَرِيرٍ إِلَّا أَنَّهُمْ قَالُوا: ﴿مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ﴾ الدُّنْيَا ﴿وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ﴾ الْآخِرَةُ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: "مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَعَنْ أَيْمَانِهِمْ": حَيْثُ يُبْصِرُونَ، "وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ وَعَنْ شَمَائِلِهِمْ": حَيْثُ لَا يُبْصِرُونَ.

وَاخْتَارَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ جَمِيعُ طُرُقِ الْخَيْرِ وَالشَّرِّ، فَالْخَيْرُ يَصُدُّهُمْ عَنْهُ، وَالشَّرُّ يُحببه لَهُمْ.

وَقَالَ الْحَكَمُ بْنُ أَبَانٍ، عَنْ عِكْرِمة، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿ثمَُ لآتِيَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ وَعَنْ أَيْمَانِهِمْ وِعَنْ شَمَائِلِهِمْ﴾ وَلَمْ يَقِلْ: مِنْ فَوْقِهِمْ؛ لِأَنَّ الرَّحْمَةَ تَنْزِلُ مِنْ فَوْقِهِمْ.

وَقَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَلا تَجِدُ أَكْثَرَهُمْ شَاكِرِينَ﴾ قَالَ: مُوَحِّدِينَ.

وَقَوْلُ إِبْلِيسَ هَذَا إِنَّمَا هُوَ ظَنٌّ مِنْهُ وَتَوَهُّمٌ، وَقَدْ وَافَقَ فِي هَذَا الْوَاقِعَ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ صَدَّقَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِبْلِيسُ ظَنَّهُ فَاتَّبَعُوهُ إِلا فَرِيقًا مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ * وَمَا كَانَ لَهُ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ سُلْطَانٍ إِلا لِنَعْلَمَ مَنْ يُؤْمِنُ بِالآخِرَةِ مِمَّنْ هُوَ مِنْهَا فِي شَكٍّ وَرَبُّكَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ حَفِيظٌ﴾ [سَبَأٍ: ٢٠، ٢١] .

وَلِهَذَا وَرَدَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الِاسْتِعَاذَةُ مِنْ تَسَلُّطِ الشَّيْطَانِ عَلَى الْإِنْسَانِ مِنْ جِهَاتِهِ كُلِّهَا، كَمَا قَالَ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْبَزَّارُ فِي مُسْنَدِهِ:

حَدَّثَنَا نَصْر بْنُ عَلِيٍّ، حَدَّثَنَا عَمْرُو بْنُ مُجَمِّع، عَنْ يُونُسَ بْنِ خَبَّاب، عَنِ ابْنِ جُبَيْر بْنِ مُطْعِم -يَعْنِي نَافِعَ بْنَ جُبَيْرٍ -عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ -وَحَدَّثَنَا عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ -يَعْنِي السِّجِسْتَانِيَّ -حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ جَعْفَرٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عُبَيْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عَمْرٍو، عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَبِي أُنَيْسَةَ، عَنِ يُونُسَ بْنِ خَبَّابٍ -عَنِ ابْنِ جُبَيْرِ بْنِ مُطْعِمٍ -عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: "اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ الْعَفْوَ وَالْعَافِيَةَ فِي دِينِي وَدُنْيَايَ، وَأَهْلِي وَمَالِي، اللَّهُمَّ اسْتُرْ عَوْرَتي، وَآمِنْ رَوْعَتِي وَاحْفَظْنِي مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدِي وَمِنْ خَلْفِي، وَعَنْ يَمِينِي وعن شمالي، وَمِنْ فَوْقِي، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ اللَّهُمَّ أَنْ أُغْتَال مِنْ تَحْتِي". تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ الْبَزَّارُ وَحَسَّنَهُ.

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا وَكِيع، حَدَّثَنَا عُبَادَةُ بْنُ مُسْلِمٍ الْفَزَارِيُّ، حَدَّثَنِي جُبَير بْنُ أَبِي سُلَيْمَانَ ابن جُبَيْرِ بْنِ مُطْعِمٍ، سَمِعْتُ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ يَقُولُ: لَمْ يَكُنْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ يَدْعُ هَؤُلَاءِ الدَّعَوَاتِ حِينَ يُصْبِحُ وَحِينَ يُمْسِي: "اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ الْعَافِيَةَ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ، اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ الْعَفْوَ وَالْعَافِيَةَ فِي دِينِي وَدُنْيَايَ وَأَهْلِي وَمَالِي، اللَّهُمَّ اسْتُرْ عَوَرَاتِي، وَآمِنْ رَوْعاتي، اللَّهُمَّ احْفَظْنِي مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيَّ وَمِنْ خَلْفِي، وَعَنْ يَمِينِي وعن شمالي، ومن فَوْقِي، وأعوذ بِعَظَمَتِكَ أَنْ أُغْتَالَ مِنْ تَحْتِي". قَالَ وَكِيعٌ: يَعْنِي الْخَسْفَ.

وَرَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ، وَالنَّسَائِيُّ، وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، وَابْنُ حِبَّان، وَالْحَاكِمُ مِنْ حَدِيثِ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ مُسْلِمٍ، بِهِ وَقَالَ الْحَاكِمُ: صَحِيحُ الْإِسْنَادِ.

---

## 7:18 — verse 18

### Translation

He, Exalted, confirmed upon him the curse, the expulsion, the removal, and the banishment from the abode of the highest assembly, in His saying: {Get out of it, disgraced and driven away}.

Ibn Jarir said: As for "al-madh'um," it means the one who is disgraced/reproached. Al-dha'm without doubling (of the consonant) means disgrace. It is said: "dha'ahu yadh'amuhu dha'man, so he is madh'um." And they drop the hamza and say: "dhamtuhu adhimuhu dhayman wa dhaman," and al-dham and al-dhaym are more emphatic in disgrace than al-dhamm (blame).

He said: "Al-madhur" means the one driven far away. It is the one who is banished and expelled.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: We do not know "al-madh'um" and "al-madhmum" except as one and the same.

Sufyan al-Thawri said, from Abu Ishaq, from al-Tamimi, from Ibn Abbas, regarding {Get out of it, disgraced and driven away}: he said, despised.

Ali ibn Abi Talha said, from Ibn Abbas: small and despised. Al-Suddi said: despised and expelled. Qatadah said: cursed and despised. Mujahid said: banished and expelled. Al-Rabi' ibn Anas said: madh'um means banished, and al-madhur means the one made small.

And His saying, Exalted is He: {As for those who follow you among them, I will surely fill Hell with you all together}, is like His saying: {He said: Go, and whoever among them follows you, indeed Hell is your recompense, an ample recompense. And incite whoever you can among them with your voice, and rally against them your cavalry and infantry, and share with them in wealth and children, and promise them, and Satan promises them nothing but delusion. Indeed, over My servants you have no authority, and sufficient is your Lord as a Guardian} [al-Isra: 63-65].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

أَكَّدَ تَعَالَى عَلَيْهِ اللَّعْنَةَ وَالطَّرْدَ وَالْإِبْعَادَ وَالنَّفْيَ عَنْ مَحَلِّ الْمَلَأِ الْأَعْلَى بِقَوْلِهِ: ﴿اخْرُجْ مِنْهَا مَذْءُومًا مَدْحُورًا﴾

قال ابن جرير: أما "المذؤوُم" فَهُوَ الْمَعِيبُ، وَالذَّأْمُ غَيْرُ مشدَّد: الْعَيْبُ. يُقَالُ: "ذَأَمَهُ يَذْأَمُهُ ذَأْمًا فَهُوَ مَذْءُومٌ". وَيَتْرُكُونَ الْهَمْزَ فَيَقُولُونَ: "ذمْته أَذِيمُهُ ذَيْمًا وذَاما، وَالذَّامُّ وَالذَّيْمُ أَبْلَغُ فِي الْعَيْبِ مِنَ الذَّمِّ".

قَالَ: "وَالْمَدْحُورُ": المُقْصَى. وَهُوَ الْمُبْعَدُ الْمَطْرُودُ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: مَا نَعْرِفُ الْمَذْءُومَ" وَ "الْمَذْمُومَ" إِلَّا وَاحِدًا.

وَقَالَ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، عَنِ التَّمِيمِيِّ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿اخْرُجْ مِنْهَا مَذْءُومًا مَدْحُورًا﴾ قَالَ: مَقِيتًا.

وَقَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: صَغِيرًا مَقِيتًا. وَقَالَ السُّدِّيُّ: مَقِيتًا مَطْرُودًا. وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: لَعِينًا مَقِيتًا. وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: مَنْفِيًّا مطرودًا. وقال الربيع بن أنس: مذؤوما: مَنْفِيًّا، وَالْمَدْحُورُ: الْمُصَغَّرُ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿لَمَنْ تَبِعَكَ مِنْهُمْ لأمْلأنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنْكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ﴾ كَقَوْلِهِ ﴿قَالَ اذْهَبْ فَمَنْ تَبِعَكَ مِنْهُمْ فَإِنَّ جَهَنَّمَ جَزَاؤُكُمْ جَزَاءً مَوْفُورًا * وَاسْتَفْزِزْ مَنِ اسْتَطَعْتَ مِنْهُمْ بِصَوْتِكَ وَأَجْلِبْ عَلَيْهِمْ بِخَيْلِكَ وَرَجِلِكَ وَشَارِكْهُمْ فِي الأمْوَالِ وَالأولادِ وَعِدْهُمْ وَمَا يَعِدُهُمُ الشَّيْطَانُ إِلا غُرُورًا * إِنَّ عِبَادِي لَيْسَ لَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ سُلْطَانٌ وَكَفَى بِرَبِّكَ وَكِيلا﴾ [الإسراء: ٦٣ -٦٥] .

---

## 7:19-21 — verses 19-21 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Exalted mentions that He permitted Adam, peace be upon him, and his wife [Eve] the Garden, that they might eat from it, from all its fruits, except one tree. The discussion of this has already preceded in "Surat al-Baqarah." At that point Satan envied the two of them, and strove through cunning, deception, and whispering to strip them of the blessing and fine covering they were in, and he said, falsely and slanderously: {Your Lord did not forbid you this tree except that you might not become two angels}, that is, lest you become two angels, or immortal here, and had you eaten from it, that would have come to be for you both, as in His saying: {He said, "O Adam, shall I direct you to the tree of eternity and a kingdom that does not decay?"} [Ta-Ha: 120]. That is, lest you become two angels, comparable to His saying: {Allah makes clear to you lest you go astray} [al-Nisa: 176], meaning: lest you go astray, and {And He cast into the earth firmly set mountains lest it should shake with you} [al-Nahl: 15], meaning: lest it shake with you.

Ibn Abbas and Yahya ibn Abi Kathir used to recite it: {except that you become two angels} with the lam vowelled as kasrah. The majority read it with fatha.

{And he swore to them both}, that is, he swore to them by Allah: {"Indeed, I am to you both among the sincere advisers."} For I was here before you both, and I know this place better. This is of the pattern of the mutual verb form (mufa'ala), though what is meant is only one side of it, as Khalid ibn Zuhayr, the cousin of Abu Dhu'ayb, said:

"He swore to her by Allah earnestly: 'You are indeed sweeter than manna, whenever it is gathered.'"

That is, he swore to them both by Allah [on this matter] until he deceived them. And the believer may indeed be deceived by means of Allah's name, for Satan said: I was created before you both, and I know more than you both, so follow me, and I will guide you rightly. Some of the people of knowledge used to say: "Whoever deceives us by means of Allah, we are deceived on his account."

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَذْكُرُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ أَبَاحَ لِآدَمَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَلِزَوْجَتِهِ [حَوَّاءَ] الْجَنَّةَ أَنْ يَأْكُلَا مِنْهَا مِنْ جَمِيعِ ثِمَارِهَا إِلَّا شَجَرَةً وَاحِدَةً. وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ الْكَلَامُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ فِي "سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ"، فَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ حَسَدَهُمَا الشَّيْطَانُ، وَسَعَى فِي الْمَكْرِ وَالْخَدِيعَةِ وَالْوَسْوَسَةِ ليُسلبا مَا هُمَا فِيهِ مِنَ النِّعْمَةِ وَاللِّبَاسِ الْحَسَنِ، وَقَالَ كَذِبًا وَافْتِرَاءً: مَا نَهَاكُمَا رَبُّكُمَا عَنْ أَكْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ إِلَّا لِتَكُونَا مَلَكَيْنِ أَيْ: لِئَلَّا تَكُونَا مَلَكَيْنِ، أَوْ خَالِدَيْنِ هَاهُنَا وَلَوْ أَنَّكُمَا أَكَلْتُمَا مِنْهَا لَحَصَلَ لَكُمَا ذَلِكُمَا كَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿قَالَ يَا آدَمُ هَلْ أَدُلُّكَ عَلَى شَجَرَةِ الْخُلْدِ وَمُلْكٍ لَا يَبْلَى﴾ [طه: ١٢٠] أَيْ: لِئَلَّا تَكُونَا مَلَكَيْنِ، كَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ أَنْ تَضِلُّوا﴾ [النِّسَاءِ: ١٧٦] أَيْ: لِئَلَّا تَضِلُّوا، ﴿وَأَلْقَى فِي الأرْضِ رَوَاسِيَ أَنْ تَمِيدَ بِكُمْ﴾ [النَّحْلِ: ١٥] أَيْ: لِئَلَّا تَمِيدَ بِكُمْ.

وَكَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَيَحْيَى بْنُ أبي كثير يقرآن: ﴿إِلا أَنْ تَكُونَا مَلَكَيْنِ﴾ بِكَسْرِ اللَّامِ. وَقَرَأَهُ الْجُمْهُورُ بِفَتْحِهَا.

﴿وَقَاسَمَهُمَا﴾ أَيْ: حَلَفَ لَهُمَا بِاللَّهِ: ﴿إِنِّي لَكُمَا لَمِنَ النَّاصِحِينَ﴾ فَإِنِّي مِنْ قَبْلكما هَاهُنَا، وَأَعْلَمُ بِهَذَا الْمَكَانِ، وَهَذَا مِنْ بَابِ الْمُفَاعَلَةِ وَالْمُرَادُ أَحَدُ الطَّرَفَيْنِ، كَمَا قَالَ خَالِدُ بْنُ زُهَيْرٍ، ابْنُ عَمِّ أَبِي ذُؤَيْبٍ:

وقاسَمَها بِاللَّهِ جَهْدا لأنتمُ ... أَلَذُّ مِنَ السَّلْوَى إِذْ مَا نُشُورُهَا 

أَيْ: حَلَفَ لَهُمَا بِاللَّهِ [عَلَى ذَلِكَ] حَتَّى خَدَعَهُمَا، وَقَدْ يُخْدَعُ الْمُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ، فَقَالَ: إِنِّي خُلقت قَبْلَكُمَا، وَأَنَا أَعْلَمُ مِنْكُمَا، فَاتَّبِعَانِي أُرْشِدُكُمَا. وَكَانَ بَعْضُ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ يَقُولُ: "مَنْ خَادَعَنَا بِاللَّهِ خُدعنا لَهُ".

---

## 7:22-23 — verses 22-23 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah said, from Qatadah, from al-Hasan, from Ubayy ibn Ka'b, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: Adam was a tall man, as if he were a towering palm tree, with abundant hair on his head. When he fell into the sin he fell into, his private part became exposed to him at that point, whereas before he had not seen it. So he set off fleeing through the Garden, and a tree of the trees of the Garden caught hold of his head. He said to it, "Release me." It said, "I will not release you." Then his Lord, mighty and majestic is He, called out to him: "O Adam, are you fleeing from Me?" He said, "My Lord, I felt shame before You."

Ibn Jarir and Ibn Mardawayh have related this through several routes, from al-Hasan, from Ubayy ibn Ka'b, from the Prophet ﷺ, but the mawquf (halted report, i.e. attributed only to Ubayy and not to the Prophet ﷺ) version has the more sound chain of transmission.

'Abd al-Razzaq said: Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah and Ibn al-Mubarak informed us, from al-Hasan ibn 'Umarah, from al-Minhal ibn 'Amr, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn 'Abbas, who said: The tree which Allah forbade to Adam and his wife was the ear of grain (al-sunbulah). When they ate from it, their private parts became exposed to them. What had concealed their private parts from them was their fingernails. They began to fasten together over themselves leaves of the Garden, fig leaves, sticking one to another. Adam, peace be upon him, set off fleeing through the Garden, and a tree of the Garden caught hold of his head. He was called: "O Adam, are you fleeing from Me?" He said, "No, but I felt shame before You, my Lord." He said, "Was there not, in what I granted you of the Garden and permitted you from it, sufficient scope apart from that which I forbade you?" He said, "Yes indeed, my Lord, but by Your might, I did not think that anyone would swear falsely by You." He said: this is referred to in His saying, mighty and majestic is He, {and he swore to them both, "Indeed, I am to you both among the sincere advisers"}. He said: "Then by My might, I will surely bring you down to the earth, and after that you shall not attain sustenance except through toil." He said: So he was brought down from the Garden. They used to eat from it in abundance, but he was brought down to a place without abundance of food and drink. So he was taught the craft of ironworking and commanded to till the soil. He tilled and sowed, then watered, until the crop matured, then he harvested it, then threshed it, then winnowed it, then ground it, then kneaded it, then baked it, then ate it, but he did not obtain it until he had reached the point Allah willed him to reach.

Al-Thawri said, from Ibn Abi Layla, from al-Minhal ibn 'Amr, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn 'Abbas, regarding {and they both began to fasten together over themselves leaves of the Garden}: he said, fig leaves. This is sound as far as it goes back to him.

Mujahid said: they began to fasten together over themselves leaves of the Garden in the manner of a garment.

Wahb ibn Munabbih said concerning His saying, {stripping from them both their garment}: he said, the garment of Adam and Eve was a light over their private parts, so that this one did not see the private part of that one, nor did that one see the private part of this one. When they ate from the tree, their private parts became exposed to them. Ibn Jarir related this with a sound chain going back to him.

'Abd al-Razzaq said: Ma'mar informed us, from Qatadah, who said: Adam said, "O my Lord, what do You think, if I repent and seek forgiveness?" He said, "Then I will admit you into the Garden." As for Iblis, he did not ask Him for repentance, but asked Him for a reprieve, and each of the two was given what he had asked for.

Ibn Jarir said: al-Qasim related to us, al-Husayn related to us, 'Abbad ibn al-'Awwam related to us, from Sufyan ibn Husayn, from Ya'la ibn Muslim, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn 'Abbas, who said: When Adam ate from the tree, it was said to him, "Why did you eat from the tree which I forbade you?" He said, "Eve ordered me to." He said, "Then I have made her recompense for that: that she shall not conceive except with hardship, and shall not give birth except with hardship." He said: at that Eve cried out. So it was said to her, "The crying out shall be upon you and upon your offspring."

Al-Dahhak ibn Muzahim said, concerning His saying, {Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves, and if You do not forgive us and have mercy upon us, we will surely be among the losers}: these are the words which Adam received from his Lord, mighty and majestic is He.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ أَبِي عَرُوبَة، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ، عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، عَنْ أُبَيِّ بْنِ كَعْبٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: كَانَ آدَمُ رَجُلًا طُوَالا كَأَنَّهُ نَخْلَةٌ سَحُوق، كَثِيرُ شَعْرِ الرَّأْسِ. فَلَمَّا وَقَعَ بِمَا وَقَعَ بِهِ مِنَ الْخَطِيئَةِ، بَدَتْ لَهُ عَوْرَتُهُ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ، وَكَانَ لَا يَرَاهَا. فَانْطَلَقَ هَارِبًا فِي الْجَنَّةِ فَتَعَلَّقَتْ بِرَأْسِهِ شَجَرَةٌ مِنْ شَجَرِ الْجَنَّةِ، فَقَالَ لَهَا: أَرْسِلِينِي. فَقَالَتْ: إِنِّي غَيْرُ مُرْسِلَتِكَ. فَنَادَاهُ رَبُّهُ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: يَا آدَمُ، أَمِنِّي تَفِرُّ؟ قَالَ: رَبِّ إِنِّي اسْتَحْيَيْتُكَ. 

وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ، وَابْنُ مَرْدُويه مِنْ طُرُق، عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، عَنْ أُبَيِّ بْنِ كَعْبٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ، وَالْمَوْقُوفُ أَصَحُّ إِسْنَادًا. 

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ: أَنْبَأَنَا سُفْيَانُ بْنُ عُيَيْنَةَ وَابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ، عَنِ الْحَسَنِ بْنِ عِمَارَةَ، عَنِ المِنْهَال بْنِ عَمْرٍو، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جبير، عن ابن عباس قال: كانت الشَّجَرَةُ الَّتِي نَهَى اللَّهُ عَنْهَا آدَمَ وَزَوْجَتَهُ، السُّنْبُلَةَ. فَلَمَّا أَكَلَا مِنْهَا بَدَتْ لَهُمَا سَوْآتُهُمَا، وَكَانَ الَّذِي وَارَى عَنْهُمَا مِنْ سَوْآتِهِمَا أَظْفَارَهُمَا، وَطَفِقَا يَخْصِفَانِ عَلَيْهِمَا مِنْ وَرَقِ الْجَنَّةِ وَرقَ التِّينِ، يَلْزَقَانِ بَعْضَهُ إِلَى بَعْضٍ. فَانْطَلَقَ آدَمُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، مُوَلِّيًا فِي الْجَنَّةِ، فَعَلِقَتْ بِرَأْسِهِ شَجَرَةٌ مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ، فَنَادَاهُ: يَا آدَمُ، أَمِنِّي تَفِرُّ؟ قَالَ: لَا وَلَكِنِّي اسْتَحْيَيْتُكَ يَا رَبِّ. قَالَ: أَمَا كَانَ لَكَ فِيمَا مَنَحْتُكَ مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ وَأَبَحْتُكَ مِنْهَا مَنْدُوحَةً، عَمَّا حَرَّمْتُ عَلَيْكَ. قَالَ: بَلَى يَا رَبِّ، وَلَكِنْ وَعِزَّتِكَ مَا حَسِبْتُ أَنَّ أَحَدًا يَحْلِفُ بِكَ كَاذِبًا. قَالَ: وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ ﴿وَقَاسَمَهُمَا إِنِّي لَكُمَا لَمِنَ النَّاصِحِينَ﴾ قَالَ: فَبِعِزَّتِي لَأُهْبِطَنَّكَ إِلَى الْأَرْضِ، ثُمَّ لَا تَنَالُ الْعَيْشَ إِلَّا كَدا. قَالَ: فَأُهْبِطَ مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ، وَكَانَا يَأْكُلَانِ مِنْهَا رَغَدًا، فَأُهْبِطَ إِلَى غَيْرِ رَغَدٍ مِنْ طَعَامٍ وَشَرَابٍ، فعُلّم صَنْعَةَ الْحَدِيدِ، وَأُمِرَ بِالْحَرْثِ، فَحَرَثَ وَزَرَعَ ثُمَّ سَقَى، حَتَّى إِذَا بَلَغَ حَصَدَ، ثُمَّ دَاسَهُ، ثُمَّ ذَرّاه، ثُمَّ طَحَنَهُ، ثُمَّ عَجَنَهُ، ثُمَّ خَبَزَهُ، ثُمَّ أَكَلَهُ، فَلَمْ يَبْلُغْهُ حَتَّى بَلَغَ مِنْهُ مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ أَنْ يَبْلُغَ وَقَالَ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنِ ابْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، عَنِ الْمِنْهَالِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَطَفِقَا يَخْصِفَانِ عَلَيْهِمَا مِنْ وَرَقِ الْجَنَّةِ﴾ قَالَ: وَرَقُ التِّينِ. صَحِيحٌ إِلَيْهِ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: جَعَلَا يَخْصِفَانِ عَلَيْهِمَا مِنْ وَرَقِ الْجَنَّةِ كَهَيْئَةِ الثَّوْبِ.

وَقَالَ وَهْب بْنُ مُنَبِّه فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿يَنزعُ عَنْهُمَا لِبَاسَهُمَا﴾ قَالَ: كَانَ لِبَاسُ آدَمَ وَحَوَّاءَ نُورًا عَلَى فُرُوجِهِمَا، لَا يَرَى هَذَا عَوْرَةَ هَذِهِ، وَلَا هَذِهِ عَوْرَةَ هَذَا. فَلَمَّا أَكَلَا مِنَ الشَّجَرَةِ بَدَتْ لَهُمَا سَوْآتُهُمَا. رَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ بِإِسْنَادٍ صَحِيحٍ إِلَيْهِ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ: أَخْبَرَنَا مَعْمَر، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ آدَمُ: أَيْ رَبِّ، أَرَأَيْتَ إِنْ تُبْتُ وَاسْتَغْفَرْتُ؟ قَالَ: إِذًا أُدْخِلُكَ الْجَنَّةَ. وَأَمَّا إِبْلِيسُ فَلَمْ يَسْأَلْهُ التَّوْبَةَ، وَسَأَلَهُ النَّظْرَةَ، فَأُعْطِيَ كل واحد منهما الذي سأله.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا الْقَاسِمُ، حَدَّثَنَا الْحُسَيْنُ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبَّاد بْنُ العَوَّام، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ بْنِ حُسَيْنٍ، عَنْ يَعْلَى بْنِ مُسْلِمٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: لَمَّا أَكَلَ آدَمُ مِنَ الشَّجَرَةِ قِيلَ لَهُ: لِمَ أَكَلْتَ مِنَ الشَّجَرَةِ الَّتِي نَهَيْتُكَ عَنْهَا. قَالَ: حَوَّاءُ. أَمَرَتْنِي. قَالَ: فَإِنِّي قَدْ أَعْقَبْتُهَا أَنْ لَا تَحْمِلَ إِلَّا كَرْها، وَلَا تَضَعَ إِلَّا كَرْها. قَالَ: فرنَّت عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ حَوَّاءُ. فَقِيلَ لَهَا: الرَّنَّةُ عَلَيْكِ وَعَلَى وَلَدِكِ 

وَقَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ بْنُ مُزَاحِم فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿رَبَّنَا ظَلَمْنَا أَنْفُسَنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ تَغْفِرْ لَنَا وَتَرْحَمْنَا لَنَكُونَنَّ مِنَ الْخَاسِرِينَ﴾ هِيَ الْكَلِمَاتُ الَّتِي تَلَقَّاهَا آدَمُ مِنْ رَبِّهِ [عَزَّ وَجَلَّ]

---

## 7:24-25 — verses 24-25 (shared commentary)

### Translation

It is said: what is meant by the address in {Descend} is Adam, Eve, Iblis, and the serpent. Some of them did not mention the serpent, and God knows best.

The main basis of the enmity is Adam and Iblis. That is why the Almighty said in Surat Ta Ha: {He said, "Descend from it, all of you"} [verse 123], and Eve is subordinate to Adam. As for the serpent, if its mention is correct, then it is subordinate to Iblis.

The commentators have mentioned the places to which each of them descended, but the substance of those reports goes back to Israelite traditions (Isra'iliyyat), and God knows best their soundness. Had there been any benefit for those who are morally accountable, in matters of their religion or their worldly affairs, in specifying those locations, God Almighty would have mentioned them in His Book, or His Messenger ﷺ would have mentioned them.

Regarding His saying: {And for you on earth is a settlement and provision for a time}, meaning: a dwelling place and lifespans appointed to known terms, which the Pen has already recorded, which the divine decree has enumerated, and which have been written down in the First Book. Ibn Abbas said: {a settlement} means the graves. And from him also: the surface of the earth and beneath it. Both reports were narrated by Ibn Abi Hatim.

Regarding His saying: {He said, "In it you will live, and in it you will die, and from it you will be brought out"}, this is like His saying: {From it We created you, and into it We will return you, and from it We will bring you out another time} [Ta Ha: 55]. The Almighty informs that He has made the earth an abode for the children of Adam for the duration of worldly life. In it is their living, and in it is their dying and their graves, and from it is their being raised up for the Day of Resurrection, on which God will gather the first and the last, and will recompense each according to his deeds.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قِيلَ: الْمُرَادُ بِالْخِطَابِ فِي ﴿اهْبِطُوا﴾ آدَمُ، وَحَوَّاءُ، وَإِبْلِيسُ، وَالْحَيَّةُ. وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرِ الْحَيَّةَ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَالْعُمْدَةُ فِي الْعَدَاوَةِ آدَمُ وَإِبْلِيسُ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي سُورَةِ "طه" قَالَ: ﴿اهْبِطَا مِنْهَا جَمِيعًا﴾ [الْآيَةَ: ١٢٣] وَحَوَّاءُ تَبَعٌ لِآدَمَ. وَالْحَيَّةُ -إِنْ كَانَ ذِكْرُهَا صَحِيحًا -فَهِيَ تَبَعٌ لِإِبْلِيسَ.

وَقَدْ ذَكَرَ الْمُفَسِّرُونَ الْأَمَاكِنَ الَّتِي هَبَطَ فِيهَا كُلٌّ مِنْهُمْ، وَيَرْجِعُ حَاصِلُ تِلْكَ الْأَخْبَارِ إِلَى الْإِسْرَائِيلِيَّاتِ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِصِحَّتِهَا. وَلَوْ كَانَ فِي تَعْيِينِ تِلْكَ الْبِقَاعِ فَائِدَةٌ تَعُودُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِينَ فِي أَمْرِ دِينِهِمْ، أَوْ دُنْيَاهُمْ، لَذَكَرَهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ أَوْ رَسُولُهُ ﷺ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلَكُمْ فِي الأرْضِ مُسْتَقَرٌّ وَمَتَاعٌ إِلَى حِينٍ﴾ أَيْ: قَرَارٌ وَأَعْمَارٌ مَضْرُوبَةٌ إِلَى آجَالٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ، قَدْ جَرَى بِهَا الْقَلَمُ، وَأَحْصَاهَا الْقَدَرُ، وَسُطِّرَتْ فِي الْكِتَابِ الْأَوَّلِ. وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿مُسْتَقَرٌّ﴾ الْقُبُورُ. وَعَنْهُ: وَجْهُ الْأَرْضِ وَتَحْتَهَا. رَوَاهُمَا ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿قَالَ فِيهَا تَحْيَوْنَ وَفِيهَا تَمُوتُونَ وَمِنْهَا تُخْرَجُونَ﴾ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَاكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُكُمْ وَمِنْهَا نُخْرِجُكُمْ تَارَةً أُخْرَى﴾ [طه: ٥٥] يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ يَجْعَلُ الْأَرْضَ دَارًا لِبَنِي آدَمَ مُدَّةَ الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا، فِيهَا مَحْيَاهُمْ وَفِيهَا مَمَاتُهُمْ وَقُبُورُهُمْ، وَمِنْهَا نُشُورُهُمْ لِيَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ الَّذِي يَجْمَعُ اللَّهُ فِيهِ الْأَوَّلِينَ وَالْآخِرِينَ، وَيُجَازِي كُلًّا بِعَمَلِهِ.

---

## 7:26 — verse 26

### Translation

Blessed and Exalted is He, He confers a favor upon His servants by what He has provided for them of clothing and rīsh (adornment). The "clothing" mentioned here is for covering the private parts, which are the shameful parts, while riyash and rīsh refers to what one adorns oneself with outwardly. The first is among the necessities, while rīsh is among the completions and additions.

Ibn Jarir said: "riyash" in the speech of the Arabs means furnishings and household goods, and what appears of garments.

Ali ibn Abi Talha said, from Ibn Abbas, and al-Bukhari related it from him: riyash means wealth. Mujahid, Urwah ibn al-Zubayr, al-Suddi, and al-Dahhak said likewise.

Al-Awfi said, from Ibn Abbas: "riyash" means clothing, comfortable living, and blessing.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: "riyash" means beauty.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Abu al-Ala al-Shami said: Abu Umamah put on a new garment, and when it reached his collarbone he said: "Praise be to God who has clothed me with what I use to cover my private parts and adorn myself with in my life." Then he said: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab say: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Whoever acquires a new garment and puts it on, and says when it reaches his collarbone: 'Praise be to God who has clothed me with what I use to cover my private parts and adorn myself with in my life,' then takes the garment that has become worn out, or he said: that he has set aside, and gives it in charity, he will be under God's protection, in God's shelter, and in God's care, living and dead, [living and dead, living and dead]."

Al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah related it from the narration of Yazid ibn Harun, from Asbagh, who is Ibn Zayd al-Juhani, whom Yahya ibn Ma'in and others declared trustworthy. His teacher "Abu al-Ala al-Shami" is not known except through this hadith, but no one has authenticated it as sound. God knows best.

Imam Ahmad also said: [chain] Abu Matar said that he saw Ali, may God be pleased with him, come to a young boy and buy a shirt from him for three dirhams, and he wore it reaching from the wrists down to the ankles, saying as he wore it: "Praise be to God who has provided me with riyash by which I adorn myself among people and cover my private parts with it." He was asked: Is this something you narrate from yourself or from the Prophet of God ﷺ? He said: This is something I heard from the Messenger of God ﷺ, who used to say upon putting on clothing: "Praise be to God who has provided me with riyash by which I adorn myself among people and cover my private parts with it."

Regarding His saying, Exalted is He: {And the clothing of taqwa (God-consciousness), that is better}, some read it as "wa libasa al-taqwa" in the accusative case, while others read it in the nominative as the subject of a new clause, with {that is better} as its predicate.

The exegetes differed concerning its meaning. Ikrimah said: it is said that it is what the God-conscious will wear on the Day of Resurrection. Ibn Abi Hatim related this.

Zayd ibn Ali, al-Suddi, Qatadah, and Ibn Jurayj said: {the clothing of taqwa} means faith.

Al-Awfi said, from Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with him: {the clothing of taqwa} means righteous deeds.

Ziyad ibn Amr said, from Ibn Abbas: it is the good bearing visible upon the face.

From Urwah ibn al-Zubayr: {the clothing of taqwa} means fear of God.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: {the clothing of taqwa} means one who fears God and thereby covers his private parts, that is the clothing of taqwa.

All of these meanings are close to one another, and this is supported by the hadith that Ibn Jarir related, where he said:

[chain] al-Hasan said: I saw Uthman ibn Affan, may God be pleased with him, upon the pulpit of the Messenger of God ﷺ, wearing a garment of qūhī cloth with its button undone, and I heard him command that dogs be killed and forbid playing with pigeons. Then he said: O people, fear God regarding these hidden matters, for I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: "By the One in whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, no one ever does something in secret except that God clothes him with a garment of it openly, if it is good then good, and if it is evil then evil." Then he recited this verse: "wa riyashan" and he did not recite "wa rishan": {And the clothing of taqwa, that is better, that is among the signs of God}, and he said: "It is the good bearing."

Thus Ibn Jarir related it through the narration of Sulayman ibn Arqam, in which there is weakness. But the imams al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and al-Bukhari in the Book of Manners have related, through sound chains, from al-Hasan al-Basri, that he heard the Commander of the Faithful Uthman ibn Affan command the killing of dogs and the slaughtering of pigeons on a Friday upon the pulpit.

As for the marfu (elevated) version of it, the hafiz Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani related in his al-Mu'jam al-Kabir a corroborating report through another route, where he said: [chain]...

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَمْتَنُّ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى عَلَى عِبَادِهِ بِمَا جَعَلَ لَهُمْ مِنَ اللباس والريش فاللباس المذكور هاهنا لستر العورات -وهي السوآت وَالرِّيَاشُ وَالرِّيشُ: هُوَ مَا يُتَجَمَّلُ بِهِ ظَاهِرًا، فَالْأَوَّلُ مِنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ، وَالرِّيشُ مِنَ التَّكَمُّلَاتِ وَالزِّيَادَاتِ.

قَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: "الرِّيَاشُ" فِي كَلَامِ الْعَرَبِ: الْأَثَاثُ، وَمَا ظَهَرَ مِنَ الثِّيَابِ.

وَقَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ -وَحَكَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ -عَنْهُ: الرِّيَاشُ: الْمَالُ. وَكَذَا قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، وعُرْوَة بْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ، والسُّدِّي وَالضَّحَّاكُ 

وَقَالَ العَوْفي، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: "الرِّيَاشُ" اللِّبَاسُ، وَالْعَيْشُ، وَالنَّعِيمُ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: "الرِّيَاشُ": الْجَمَالُ.
